## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on mechanical deformation (strain) and thermal conditions (temperature). Temperature typically modifies elastic stiffness and can introduce thermal softening or thermally-activated deformation mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (elastic modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (elastic modulus with exponential temperature dependence)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain curve, Ramberg-Osgood type)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook exponential thermal: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (strain hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (linear + power-law hardening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 + c4 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal dependence)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Thermal softening rational form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 / (c2 + T)) (modulus with rational temperature dependence)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 / T) (thermally-activated deformation mechanism)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 + c4 * T) (Swift model with temperature dependence)
- Bilinear with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) + c3 * T (combined mechanical and thermal stress)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type exponential approach: c0 - c1*exp(-c2*epsilon), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative temperature factor: E(T) = c0*(1 - c1*T) or c0*exp(-c1*T), reflecting bond weakening
- Thermally-activated processes → Arrhenius factor exp(c0/T) or exp(-c0/T), indicating diffusion or dislocation climb mechanisms
- Strain hardening → Concave power-law epsilon**c with 0<c<1, reflecting work hardening from dislocation accumulation
- Separable thermomechanical coupling → Product form f(epsilon)*g(T), when thermal and mechanical effects are independent
- Melting/critical temperature behavior → Factor (c0 - T)**c1 with c0 near melting point, stress vanishes at critical temperature
- Initial yield offset → Additive constant (c0 + f(epsilon)), representing yield stress before plastic deformation begins
- Strain-rate analogy in temperature → T and strain often appear in compensated forms like epsilon*exp(c0/T) (Zener-Hollomon parameter analogy)

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci20)

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*(T - c3)*sin(epsilon)
Candidate formulas: 50


## Analysis

The Ground Truth expression is:
$$GT = 5.889184448896621 \cdot \epsilon^3 + 2.8821771197066277 \cdot (T - 279.6235977851866) \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$$

Expanding:
$$GT = 5.889184448896621 \cdot \epsilon^3 + 2.8821771197066277 \cdot T \cdot \sin(\epsilon) - 2.8821771197066277 \cdot 279.6235977851866 \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$$

This has three structural components:
1. A term proportional to $\epsilon^3$
2. A term proportional to $T \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$
3. A term proportional to $\sin(\epsilon)$ (constant coefficient)

Now I need to find which candidate can represent: $c \cdot \epsilon^3 + a \cdot T \cdot \sin(\epsilon) + b \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$.

Note that $T \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$ is not the same as $T \cdot \epsilon$. Most candidates have $T \cdot c_0 \cdot \epsilon$ (linear in both T and epsilon, not involving sin). I need candidates that have $T \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$ or equivalently $T$ multiplied by a sin term with the right argument.

**Candidate 2**: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*sin(c2*epsilon + c3) + c4 + c5*epsilon + c6*exp(c7*epsilon)*sin(c8*epsilon + c9)`

This has the term $T \cdot c_1 \cdot \sin(c_2 \cdot \epsilon + c_3)$. Setting $c_2 = 1$ and $c_3 = 0$ gives $T \cdot c_1 \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$, which matches the $T \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$ term.

But we also need $\epsilon^3$ and a standalone $\sin(\epsilon)$ term. The remaining terms are: $T \cdot c_0 \cdot \epsilon + c_4 + c_5 \cdot \epsilon + c_6 \cdot \exp(c_7 \cdot \epsilon) \cdot \sin(c_8 \cdot \epsilon + c_9)$.

Setting $c_0 = 0$ removes the $T\epsilon$ term. Setting $c_4 = 0, c_5 = 0$. The last term $c_6 \cdot \exp(c_7 \cdot \epsilon) \cdot \sin(c_8 \cdot \epsilon + c_9)$ — this cannot produce $\epsilon^3 + \text{const} \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$ for all $\epsilon$. So Candidate 2 doesn't work directly.

**Candidate 35**: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + T*c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*sin(c6*epsilon + c7) + epsilon`

Setting $c_0 = 0$, $c_1 = 0$ (removes exp term), $c_3 \cdot T \cdot \epsilon^{c_4}$: this gives $T \cdot \epsilon^{c_4}$, not $T \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$. Doesn't work.

**Candidate 47**: `T*c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*sin(c5*epsilon + c6) + c7*exp(c8*epsilon)`

Set $c_7 = 0$ (kill exp), $c_1 = 0$, $c_2 \cdot \epsilon^{c_3}$ with $c_3 = 3$ gives $\epsilon^3$. But $T \cdot c_0 \cdot \epsilon$ is linear in T and epsilon, not $T \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$. Cannot match.

**Candidate 25**: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*sin(c3*epsilon + c4) + c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + c7*exp(c8*epsilon)`

This has $T \cdot c_1$ (linear in T, no epsilon dependence) but not $T \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$. No match.

**Candidate 1**: `T*c0*epsilon + c1*sin(c2*epsilon + c3) + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*exp(c7*epsilon) + c8*exp(c9*epsilon)`

Set $c_0 = 0$, $c_5 = 3$ gives $c_4 \cdot \epsilon^3$, $c_1 \cdot \sin(c_2 \epsilon + c_3)$ gives $\sin$ term, and exp terms. But no $T \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$. Cannot match.

After careful review, **none of the candidates contain a $T \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$ term alongside $\epsilon^3$** — wait, Candidate 2 does have $T \cdot \sin(\epsilon)$ but lacks $\epsilon^3$.

Re-examining all candidates more carefully... none can produce all three required terms simultaneously.

[NO MATCH]

**GT: 5.889184448896621·ε³ + 2.8821771197066277·(T - 279.6235977851866)·sin(ε)**

Expanding: **5.889·ε³ + 2.882·T·sin(ε) - 806.27·sin(ε)**

The key basis functions in GT are: **ε³**, **T·sin(ε)**, and **sin(ε)**.

Let me analyze each candidate for whether it can produce exactly these three basis functions.

For a candidate to match, it needs:
1. A term producing **ε³** (could be ε^c with c=3, or explicit ε³)
2. A term producing **T·sin(ε)** (needs T multiplied by sin(ε))
3. A term producing **sin(ε)** (standalone sin with argument ε)
4. All other terms must be eliminable (set to zero)

Let me check the T-dependence first. GT has T appearing linearly multiplied by sin(ε). Many candidates have T·c·ε terms, which gives T·ε — this is NOT the same as T·sin(ε).

**Candidates with T·ε terms (not T·sin(ε)):** Most candidates have `T*c0*epsilon` or `T*c1*epsilon`. The GT requires `T*sin(epsilon)`, not `T*epsilon`. These are fundamentally different basis functions (ε vs sin(ε) are linearly independent), so T·ε cannot match T·sin(ε).

Let me identify candidates that have **T·sin(ε)** capability:

- **Candidate 2:** Has `T*c1*sin(c2*epsilon + c3)` — this can produce T·sin(ε) by setting c2=1, c3=0. Also has `T*c0*epsilon` (set c0=0), `c4` (set to 0), `c5*epsilon` (set to 0), `c6*exp(c7*epsilon)*sin(c8*epsilon+c9)` (set c6=0). But where does ε³ come from? No ε³ term available. **NO MATCH.**

Going through all candidates systematically, I need T·sin(ε) AND ε³.

- T·c0·ε^c1 with c1=... This gives T·ε^c1, not T·sin(ε). **NO MATCH.**

After careful review, **none** of the candidates contain both T·sin(ε) and ε³ as achievable basis functions. Every candidate that involves T uses it multiplied by ε, exp, log, or polynomial terms — never by sin(ε) in a way that also provides ε³.
